Foreign News

French President Doumer Dies

The People of Paris Are Shocked by This Tragedy

The Remains Will Be Buried in a State Funeral on Thursday

The President of the Senate Temporarily Assumes Presidential Powers

Reuters, London, 7th: French President Doumer succumbed to his injuries and passed away at 4:40 this morning. His family and ministers such as Taittinger were by his side. At dawn, his body was moved to the presidential palace. The French cabinet convened a special meeting this morning to discuss the state funeral and the convocation of parliament at Versailles to elect a successor president. The whole world was shocked and angered by the news of the assassination of the French president. Dignitaries from various countries telegraphed Paris to express their sympathy. In addition to grief and indignation, French newspapers unanimously expressed the opinion that France accommodates too many insidious foreigners. British newspapers detailed the assassination and offered criticism, expressing their grief and sorrow, calling Doumer a good friend of Britain and a loyal servant of France, and recounting the loss of his four sons in the Great War. The previous French president assassinated was Carnot, in 1894, at Lyon.

Reuters, Paris, 7th: At dawn today, the police chief announced outside the Beaujon Hospital, "Gentlemen, the President has just passed away." The scene was extremely tragic. Then, the President's wife led her two daughters out in tears. Someone then carried a yellow litter covered with a white cloth. Following them was General Tracouani, head of the President's military household, carrying Doumer's remains to the presidential palace. The people waiting outside the courtyard all removed their hats in tears and stood silently on both sides to let it pass. The people of Paris were shocked by this tragedy, and almost all businesses were suspended today. Countless merchants and workers gathered outside the presidential palace early in the morning. The body is now being embalmed. After that, the public will be allowed to pay their last respects to this benevolent white-bearded old man of France. According to the constitution, parliament must convene immediately to elect a successor president, but since tomorrow is the second round of voting in the election, it will not convene before Tuesday. Judging from the situation, Senate President Lebrun is likely to be elected without opposition. What impact this tragic death will have on the general election cannot be measured at present. However, since everyone regards the murderer as a madman, even if there is an impact, it will be minimal. It is still uncertain whether the members of parliament attending the convening of parliament will be the old members or the new members, as there is no precedent to follow.

Reuters, Paris, 7th: The late President Doumer will have a state funeral at Notre Dame Cathedral, scheduled for May 12 and buried in the Pantheon. No one had been buried there since the death of President Carnot, who was also assassinated in 1894. On that day, the national theater and public offices will be closed, and the whole country will fly flags at half-mast to express mourning. Civil and military officials will observe mourning for one month. On the afternoon of Sunday, the remains will be displayed in the grand hall of the presidential palace. Today, all theaters in the country have suspended performances to show respect. The famous writer Frélaut, who was shot twice while trying to seize the murderer's weapon, has had one bullet removed, while the other bullet remains in his body. He cannot sleep peacefully at night and is in a precarious state.

Havas, Paris, 7th: President Doumer passed away this morning due to his injuries. The powers of the President are temporarily assumed by the President of the Senate. Members of parliament have generally stated that the lack of a vice president in the French constitution is a real regret.

The Circumstances of the Assassination at the Venue

Reuters, Paris, 7th: According to eyewitnesses at the venue, the murderer, Gorguloff, wore dark glasses and asked the famous writer Frélaut to sign his name on three books. Frélaut agreed. President Doumer then stepped forward to greet Frélaut. At this moment, gunshots rang out, and the President fell to the ground unconscious. The Minister of Defense and the Police Chief quickly grabbed the assassin and took away his gun. The general audience initially suspected that the gunshots were the sound of a flashbulb exploding, but then a woman holding a book stained with blood ran out of the venue and exclaimed, "They are killing people!" The assassin was surrounded by an angry crowd and would have been beaten to death without police intervention. When the assassin was taken to the police station, he raised his hands to the sky in prayer, and the crowd still shouted wildly, "Kill the assassin!" The police have now detained a Swiss woman from Monaco who once lived with Gorguloff and brought her to Paris for questioning. The chairman of the Russian Emigrant Committee in France has issued an article expressing the committee's indignation at this act of violence. The police believe that Gorguloff's claim that he opposed communism may be an intentional deception. The backlash from the political violence of the Russian fascists may have a great impact on the second election on Sunday. Even if Gorguloff is indeed mentally ill, his crime may still implicate the Russian émigrés who have taken refuge in Paris and throughout France.

Comatose All Night

Succumbing to Injuries

National News Agency, Paris, 7th: Doumer was only conscious for four minutes before and after being assassinated. The rest of the time he was comatose and groaned incessantly. Doctors administered morphine from time to time, but the pain did not subside, so he did not leave a will. After the news of Doumer's death was announced, the police immediately stated that they would charge the murderer Gorguloff with first-degree murder.

National News Agency, Paris, 7th: French President Doumer was in critical condition after being attacked yesterday. At 2:30 this morning, doctors reported that the President had entered a coma. At 10:00 last night, doctors reported that his temperature was 37.2 degrees Celsius and his condition remained extremely serious. At 5:41 last night, doctors reported that the President had one bullet wound, one at the base of the skull and one in the right chest. The bleeding had stopped, but the situation was extremely serious. Two blood transfusions had been performed. He is now in a coma. It is said that the bullet that penetrated the neck went deep behind the ear and stopped in a glandular substance, which is in a very dangerous position. It is also said that the shoulder artery was ruptured by the bullet, so the bleeding did not stop. After surgery to stop the bleeding at 7:15 last night, it started bleeding again at 7:45, and a third blood transfusion was performed at 9:10. At that time, his condition seemed to have improved slightly, but he fell into a coma again at midnight.

The Murderer's Bizarre Confession

Claiming to Be a Russian Fascist

A Diary Was Found in His Pocket

Feigning Madness? Mental Derangement?

National News Agency, Paris, 7th: The murderer, Gorguloff, is still in the police station near the scene of the incident, heavily chained and interrogated overnight by the authorities. The man is a patriot, with the fantasy of becoming a Russian Mussolini or Hitler. He claims to be the creator and president of the Russian Fascist Party. He returned to Paris from Monaco on Wednesday to personally assassinate Doumer because France and other European countries and the United States were assisting Soviet Russia and providing money, which was harming Russia. He also muttered to himself that France and the United States were the great enemies of Russia. He also said that he had no personal hatred for Doumer and had no intention of harming him at first, but when he saw France preparing to join hands with Soviet Russia, he took this action to make France declare war on the communists. He also claimed that this was entirely his own doing and had no accomplices. However, his confessions were inconsistent and often discontinuous. He also claimed to be the president of the Russian Fascist Republican Democratic Party, because France had already been red-ified, just like the United States had become a great enemy of past and future Russia, so he took this action. Gorguloff is a White Russian who yearns for his homeland and has gone mad. He is 37 years old, a medical practitioner, and came to Paris two years ago. He was very active among the White Russians at one point and was deported from Czechoslovakia for inciting everywhere. He came to Paris from Monaco this time, and his wife is still in Monaco and has been arrested. The police are investigating whether there are any accomplices.

Reuters, Paris, 6th: The murderer who assassinated President Doumer was neatly dressed. In the police station, he confessed that he was a Russian patriot and said, "I know you will kill me, but I am doing what I have to do, it is my responsibility. I greatly admire the character of Hitler in Germany and Mussolini in Italy, but I have never received their assistance." The assassin's name is Gorguloff. In his pocket, there was a blue diary with the inscription "The confession of Gorguloff, the killer of the French President." Gorguloff was born in Rabenskaya in 1895. According to him, the reason he killed the French President was because France was aiding Bolshevism and the West was subsidizing Soviet Russia to promote Bolshevism. Gorguloff also claimed to be the former chairman of the Russian Fascist Party and came from Monaco to assassinate the French President. Gorguloff studied medicine in Brussels.

Reuters, Paris, 7th: The diary found in Gorguloff's pocket contained words such as "I will kidnap Lindbergh's child and educate him to become a Russian terrorist." Three psychiatrists are currently examining the assassin. Official sources say that it is still doubtful whether Gorguloff is feigning madness, but it has been determined that he formerly belonged to the Communist Party.

National Government Sends Condolences

Reuters, Nanjing, 7th: Chairman Lin of the National Government and Foreign Minister Luo have both telegraphed the French government to express condolences on the death of President Doumer. Upon receiving Reuters' telegram reporting the President's attack, Foreign Minister Luo immediately telegraphed the Chinese Embassy in Paris, ordering them to express condolences on behalf of the National Government and wish him a speedy recovery.

Havas, Paris, 6th: The news of President Doumer's assassination spread like wildfire, shocking the world. King George V of England immediately telegraphed Mrs. Doumer and Taittinger to express his condolences. French Ambassador to England, Froulliveau, a close friend of the President, went to Buckingham Palace in the afternoon to pay his respects to the King and was immediately received. German President Hindenburg and Prime Minister Brüning also telegraphed the French government. Berlin newspapers published special editions to report the assassination. The Spanish government, wishing to await news, ordered the Chamber of Deputies to delay its meeting by one hour. When the news arrived in Geneva, the Committee on Defense Expenditures of the Disarmament Conference was in session. At the suggestion of the German representative, the meeting was adjourned to express shared indignation.

French Minister to China Promoted

Doumer's Last Official Act

Reuters, Paris, 7th: According to the official gazette, President Doumer presided over a cabinet meeting yesterday and decided to promote the French Minister to China, Wilden, to first-class minister. This was Doumer's last official act.

The Life of Doumer

Served in Important Positions During His Lifetime

Four Sons Died in the European War

President Doumer was born on February 22, 1856, in Aurillac, studied law, and after graduation, soon became the secretary of Mr. Floquet, the Speaker of the House of Representatives. He was then elected as a member of the House of Representatives. From 1897 to 1902, Doumer was the Governor-General of French Vietnam. After leaving office in 1902, he returned to France and re-entered the House of Representatives, serving as Speaker of the House from 1905 to 1906. In 1912, he was elected as a Senator for Corsica and was re-elected in each subsequent term. During the European War, he was entrusted with important tasks in Russia. From 1917 to 1926, he joined several cabinets. When Briand was Prime Minister, Doumer was the Minister of Finance. In 1927, Doumer was elected as the President of the Senate. On May 13, 1931, he was elected as the 13th President of France. This year, he is 76 years old. Doumer was a member of the left-wing Democratic Party. All four of his sons died in the European War, and the French people mourned them, naming a street "The Four Sons of President Doumer" to commemorate them forever. Doumer wrote many books, including one specifically about Vietnam. Mr. Fallières, who was injured at the same time as the President, was formerly a naval officer. After retiring, he engaged in writing novels and enjoyed a high reputation in the French literary world, having written many novels about the Far East. (Havas News Agency)

Important News

Chinese Staff of the League of Nations Investigation Team Returns to Beiping

Heavily Monitored in Shenyang

Journey to Changchun Also Restricted

Forced to Return in Two Batches

Beiping Correspondence: The League of Nations Investigation Team departed from Shenyang by special train for Changchun the day before yesterday (the 2nd). Due to restrictions imposed by the Japanese, the Chinese representatives who accompanied them were limited to Gu Weijun, secretaries Yang Chengji and Shi Zhaokui, specialized committee members Liu Chongjie and Chen Liting, and consultant Ho Ping-yin, a total of seven people. The rest returned south in two batches on the 30th of last month and the 2nd of this month. The first batch, consisting of hospitality director Yan Enjun, secretary Yang Jingbin, committee members Liu Guangpei, Gu Zhizhong, and Xie Enzeng, arrived in Dalian on the evening of the 1st. Liu Guangpei temporarily stayed in Dalian due to business, and boarded a ship from Dalian directly back to Shanghai. Gu Zhizhong, Yang Jingbin, and Xie Enzeng arrived in Tianjin on the 2nd. Gu and Yang took the Jinpu train back to Shanghai on the 3rd, and Xie returned to Beiping at 12:10 AM on the 3rd. In addition, people such as Ge Gongzhen, Bao Jingan, and Chen Yichun should arrive in Beiping today or tomorrow, barring any delays en route. It is heard that after the investigation team arrived in the Northeast, they were closely monitored by the Japanese, and the Chinese representatives were treated with particular discourtesy. When taking the special train from Dalian to Shenyang, the rooms prepared on the train allocated Lord Lytton and the committee members to the foremost carriages, while the Chinese representatives were placed in the last, with the Japanese representatives in the middle, to isolate them and prevent contact between our representatives and the investigation team. After arriving in Shenyang, the Japanese immediately claimed to have prepared rooms in the Yamato Hotel, but only booked four rooms for the twenty-odd Chinese representatives, forcing our representatives to mostly find accommodation in the Orient Hotel. However, all room and board expenses, even for the rooms they booked, were paid by our representatives themselves. The day after arriving in Shenyang, a large number of Japanese detectives were dispatched to separately monitor the personnel, with two detectives monitoring one person, and four detectives monitoring those of slightly greater importance. The movements of our representatives were particularly difficult, with detectives closely following them whenever they went in or out. If they conversed with local friends on the street or had any interaction, their friends would be arrested immediately. When the investigation team left Shenyang for Changchun, our representatives originally intended to go with them, but due to repeated refusals from the Japanese, they were limited to only six people accompanying Gu Weijun. Those who could not go with them originally intended to wait in Shenyang until the team returned to Shenyang, and then return to Beiping together. However, the Japanese again strongly opposed this, claiming that if a part of our representatives were in Shenyang, it would still be a nuisance to monitor them. The team had no choice but to take a detour through Dalian and return south in succession. The investigation team's work in Shenyang, apart from five talks with Honjō, did not involve meeting with any Chinese officials. Therefore, apart from interviews with consuls from various countries and foreign merchants, the materials obtained were rarely more accurate. Lytton had very much wanted to talk to Zang Shiyi, but the Japanese did not want Zang to meet with the investigation team alone, so it did not happen. In addition, there were also Han Chinese traitors posing as representatives of merchants and farmers who visited the investigation team, all making statements flattering to the Japanese. One day, Lytton planned to go to Beiling to play golf, and the Japanese, upon hearing this, hired a large number of hoodlums, giving each of them five Japanese yen and holding small petition flags, waiting at Beiling. As a result, Lytton was unable to go due to business, and the Japanese's farcical trick did not succeed. (4th)

May Fifth Memorial Meeting in Luoyang

Lin Sen: The Meaning of "The World is for All"

Jiao Yitang: Restoring Inherent Civilization

Ju Zheng: Long-Term Resistance Will Surely Lead to Victory

Luoyang News: On the 5th, the National Government held a May Fifth Memorial Meeting, and Chairman Lin and others gave speeches, which are recorded below.

Lin Sen: Briefly stated, today is May 5th, which is the anniversary of the Premier taking office as the Extraordinary President in Guangzhou in the tenth year of the Republic. Today, we are holding a memorial meeting here, recalling the situation of the Premier's inauguration on that day, which was realized after many twists and turns and many difficulties. Because at that time, many people did not understand the meaning of the Premier's inauguration, they held opposing views. In fact, the only will of the Premier at that time was to unify China, actively launch the Northern Expedition, remove the obstacles to the revolution, and consolidate the foundation of the Republic of China. Based on this will, the Premier launched the Northern Expedition as the first step after taking office as Extraordinary President, hoping to implement his proposition of true unification, without any selfishness or consideration of rights in between. This point can be clearly seen from the fact that the Premier ceded his position to Yuan Shikai in the first year of the Republic. When the Premier took the position of Provisional President in the first year of the Republic, he ceded his position to Yuan Shikai because the policy was fundamentally unworkable. At that time, many comrades did not understand the Premier's meaning and advised him against it, because at that time, a part of the armed comrades in the north and a part of the non-comrade soldiers all expressed support for the republic, and it was not necessary to cede the position to Yuan. However, the Premier believed that if his ambitions could not be realized and the republic had someone to support it, then success did not have to be achieved by himself, and he eventually ceded the position of President. This shows the Premier's great public-spiritedness. From this point, we can see that the Premier's taking the position of Extraordinary President was not to increase his own position in any way. His concession to Yuan Shikai in the first year and his taking office as Extraordinary President in the tenth year, although the situation was different, the spirit was consistent, that is, entirely for the sake of the public, wanting to seek unification for the country and benefit for the people. Many people did not understand his painstaking efforts of not hesitating to sacrifice and not shirking labor. Today, among the comrades present, there are also those who know this situation, who know the various pains and twists and turns of that year. Therefore, on today's anniversary, we should recall that the Premier's indomitable spirit that year was entirely selfless and for the country and the people. Now is the time when the national situation is very serious. How should we reflect deeply, how should we fully understand, and how should we strive to implement the legacy shown by the Premier during his lifetime, so as not to fail the meaning of today's memorial?

Jiao Yitang: Briefly stated, today's May Fifth Festival is the anniversary of the inauguration of the Constitutional Protection President in Guangzhou. The establishment of a country is entirely dependent on law. Without law or without obeying the law, there is no country. After the establishment of the Republic of China, there was originally law, but because people often destroyed the law, it has led to years of internal strife, and now it has formed a major national crisis, leading to the relocation of the capital to Luoyang and the relocation of the secondary capital to Xi'an. In the future, we must not only abide by the law to stabilize the foundation of the country, but also revive the country by restoring the inherent civilization of China, as the Premier said. We must learn from the meaning of Duke Zhou's instruction to King Cheng to train the people, to organize local self-government at the lower level, to quickly restore the Zhou rites, and to use the Wu, Liang, Zu, Lü, Shi, and Jun system to organize people. When the country is in trouble, this can be used as an army, and when there is no trouble, it can be used for farming. We should use the Zhou Dynasty's system of state, party, clan, village, and neighborhood to organize families, on the one hand, to encourage people to produce, and on the other hand, to force people to produce. This kind of inherent civilization is indeed the foundation of governing the country and the raft of self-government, and should be vigorously implemented. Furthermore, the officials of the Zhou Dynasty were not called Baiguan but called Baigong, and the salaries of the officials were equal to the income of the farmers, so the official style was not arrogant and the people were content with their work. This is also worth borrowing from. Now that the national crisis is serious, everyone should firmly adhere to the legacy and strive for the country, so as not to fail the Premier's lifelong advocacy of abiding by the law to serve the country and restoring the inherent civilization.

Ju Zheng: Briefly stated, the Premier's taking the position of Extraordinary President that year was not a matter of increasing his own position, but to shoulder the responsibility that should be taken for transforming the country. The Premier's policy at that time was to advocate the Northern Expedition in the military to seek national unification, and to advocate equal rights and decentralized governance among the provinces in politics, because China is vast and populous, and if the powers of each province are centralized in the central government, there will definitely be many inconveniences in governance. Therefore, the Premier strongly advocated equal rights and decentralized governance among the provinces, but in reality, it was to return to unification. After he took office as Extraordinary President, he immediately sent troops to Hunan to launch the Northern Expedition. Coincidentally, at that time, the Hunan Provincial Assembly had a system of self-selecting the provincial governor, and the Premier thought it was feasible, so he wanted to promote this system to all provinces in order to accelerate the realization of people's governance. This is the first point. Secondly, at that time, there were many troops in various provinces, and the Premier wanted to find a way to absorb this excess amount of troops, so he created the engineering corps system and the militia system, such as the ancient Tuntian system, to gradually transform all the troops into industrial and agricultural workers. In addition, there were also detailed plans and explanations for local autonomy, the main purpose of which was entirely based on people's ownership, governance, and enjoyment, and he wanted to unify China without using force. This is the second point. All this shows the Premier's dedication to the country and his responsible spirit. His resolute taking of the position of Extraordinary President on this day in the tenth year of the Republic was also for this reason. Today, we are holding a memorial here, unfortunately just in the period of national crisis, which makes us feel infinitely saddened. However, we must clarify this issue with Japan. If we do not determine a proper policy for future relations with Japan, the harm will be incalculable. I believe that if we can persist in long-term resistance in the future, the final victory will surely belong to us, because Japan is a small country with a large population, limited food, and the domestic situation is extremely complicated. The intellectual and economic circles are exposing an unadjusted state everywhere. In terms of its economy, Japan's national expenditure reaches 1.7 billion yuan per year, or at least 1.6 billion yuan, while on the revenue side, taxes account for only a very small part, and most of it relies on donations from the surpluses of industry and commerce. If our country can engage in long-term resistance with it, Japan will be greatly affected. Therefore, our country's resistance to Japan now does not lie in temporary military struggles, but in long-term resistance. I hope that comrades will make up their minds together to prepare for resistance and realize resistance.

Exemption of Export Duties on Raw Silk from Jiangsu Province

The Government Agrees to Subsidize 100 Taels of Promotion Expenses per Picul

In recent years, the silk and cocoon industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang has increased exports through improved silkworm breeding. Unexpectedly, the purchasing power of Europe and the United States is weak, and the price of Japanese silk has fallen. China is suffering from natural and man-made disasters, and people cannot even afford to buy cloth, let alone silk. Therefore, this year's stock of raw silk has reached more than 20,000 piculs, and the stock of silkworm cocoons has reached 100,000 stones. If we do not find ways to promote sales, it will be even more difficult to sell the new spring cocoons. Gu Zhutong, Chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and He Yushu, Director of the Department of Industry, went to Beijing twice to negotiate an increase in the import tax on rayon and the abolition of the export tax on Chinese natural silk, in order to seek a fundamental solution. It is now heard that Mr. He telegraphed from Beijing to the province that the export tax exemption has been obtained, and the government will subsidize 100 taels of promotion expenses per picul of raw silk. The cocoon market in the Suzhou-Wuxi area has shown signs of activity upon receiving this news. This is the most valuable measure taken by the Jiangsu Provincial Government since its reorganization in terms of people's livelihood, which can increase the production of farmers in the entire Jiangnan area and a part of Jiangbei. However, the increase in the import tax on rayon still needs to be discussed.

Thief Jumps Off a Vehicle and Escapes (Wuxi Correspondence) Lu Deguan, a villager near Anzhen in the eighth district of the county, was killed by bandits last year, and his body was buried to cover up the traces. Later, Zhu Meiji, the security chief of the district, captured three bandits, Wang Xiaomei, Pan Fulang, and Du Xiaoer, and recovered Lu's remains. The county court sentenced Wang Xiaomei to death, and Pan Fulang and Du Xiaoer to twelve years of imprisonment each. Wang Xiaomei refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the Suzhou High Court. Yesterday (the 5th) at around 7:00 AM, three bailiffs from the Wuxi County Court, Zhao Chengyu, Zhou Fuzhen, and Hu Ren, took a vehicle in Suzhou to escort Pan Fulang, Du Xiaoer, and two other human trafficking suspects to Wuxi. When the vehicle was about to arrive at the Wuxi station, the bandit Pan suddenly jumped out of the hole and escaped without a trace. Bailiff Zhao and others were unable to pursue him and reported to Chief Prosecutor Zhou Erkai for handling. After Zhou opened the court, he ordered the arrest of Zhao and the other two and ordered the officers to arrest the fugitive.

Multiple Deaths by Drowning at Yiling Broken Bridge (Yangzhou Correspondence) Yiling Town, located in the eastern countryside of this county, holds a market once a year on the 28th day of the third month of the lunar calendar, as well as a god-welcoming and competitive event, which is extremely lively. Yesterday (the 3rd) was another meeting day, and pedestrians came and went, shoulder to shoulder. Unexpectedly, in the afternoon of that day, the bridge in the town suddenly broke due to the large number of pedestrians, and more than a hundred people fell under the bridge at that time. After the various agencies in the town tried to salvage the people, many were rescued, but not a few drowned. After the Jiangdu County Government received the news, it believed that the chief of the public security bureau of the town did not prevent the event in advance and did not take precautions against danger in time, which was truly inexcusable. It specially ordered Chen Xun of the Public Security Bureau to severely punish him and sent Construction Chief Xiao Zicai to investigate and review the matter.

Fire at the God of Wealth Temple (Ningbo Correspondence) The God of Wealth Temple on the north bank of the Yong River has been built for more than 200 years and is a large building in northern Yong. The Yongbei Kindergarten and the Ningbo Minguo Daily News Editorial Department are both attached to it. Unexpectedly, at around 9:00 PM yesterday (the 5th), the kitchen of the kindergarten suddenly caught fire due to carelessness. The fire was very fierce and unapproachable. It took about an hour to put it out. The main hall and the side rooms on both sides of the temple were completely burned down. The staff bedrooms and accumulated reports of the Minguo Daily News were also destroyed. The total loss is estimated to be about 20,000 yuan.

Relief for Flood Victims in the Lower River Region Completed (Nantong Correspondence) In the autumn of last year, Nantong established a reception center for flood victims from the lower river region north of the Yangtze River, accommodating more than 2,000 male and female flood victims, according to provincial orders. Now, the province's relief efforts have been cut off, and local subsidies are difficult to raise. After a resolution by the Relief Affairs Conference, the flood victims will be completely assisted in returning to their hometowns, and a report will be submitted to the province on the 6th to abolish the reception center.

Department of Education Rules on Disputes Over School Property (Nantong Correspondence) The dispute between the Nantong County Education Bureau and the Xinhua Soap Factory over school property has not been resolved for four years. The Department of Education has now ruled that the original disposition regarding the county government sending personnel to jointly receive the property with the Education Bureau should be revoked, and the Nantong County Education Bureau should file an administrative appeal according to law.

Japanese Praise its Great Diplomatic Success

Osaka Asahi Shimbun, Geneva dispatch: Since the British Ambassador to China advised his government to advocate the principle of localism in the Sino-Japanese armistice negotiations, the Continuing Committee on the 26th did not have any objections and recognized that negotiations should be conducted directly between the parties concerned on the ground, which did not violate the resolution of the General Assembly. This is considered very satisfactory for Japan. Currently, the League of Nations Secretariat is gradually showing a harmonious attitude towards the Japanese government in order to solve the aftermath of the situation. As for the results of the Continuing Committee, only small countries harbor dissatisfaction. This is the result of the joint suppression of small countries by major countries such as Britain, the United States, and France. Therefore, even if they still have the idea of retaliation if they have any opportunities in the future, they can't do anything about it. Moreover, the negotiations have actually been completed, and they can no longer intervene. This can be said to be a great diplomatic success for our country, and the small countries that echo and follow can only succumb, even if they show dissatisfaction.

Tokyo Asahi Shimbun: After the Armistice Agreement Drafting Committee amended Article 4 on the 27th, a new note was added: "If one of the Sino-Japanese parties neglects to implement the Armistice Agreement, the Mixed Committee may draw the attention of the parties concerned to this fact." Regarding this point, China's previous stubborn insistence on wanting our government to clearly indicate the time for the withdrawal of troops has also been invisibly eliminated. However, Chinese newspapers on the 28th unanimously criticized this point, saying, "Why did the National Government approve such a proposal? If so, the land of Jiangnan will be occupied by the Japanese army semi-permanently." All Chinese newspapers unanimously expressed such a view. On the other hand, English newspapers praised the approval of the Lampson plan as a great victory for Japanese diplomacy.

重光 Not Yet Out of Danger

His Temperature Reached 39 Degrees Celsius Last Night

There Is Still No Definite Certainty About His Life

Since Ambassador Shigemitsu underwent major surgery to amputate his right leg, due to anemia, his temperature soared to 40 degrees Celsius the day before yesterday, and his pulse reached 130, putting him in extreme danger for a time. After 6 PM the night before last, as a result of blood transfusions, his temperature gradually decreased, and his life began to show a glimmer of hope. His condition also improved slightly yesterday morning, with an increased appetite, and an average temperature of 38.4 degrees Celsius. However, at 2 PM yesterday afternoon, his temperature suddenly rose again to 38.9 degrees Celsius. At 4 PM, Dr. Goto performed another surgery, incising the sole of his left foot and removing four fragments, and the process went well. However, by 9 PM in the evening, his temperature had risen again to 39 degrees Celsius. Although Dr. Goto expressed an optimistic attitude to the Japanese reporters, according to the evaluation of general physicians, Ambassador Shigemitsu's life is still far from certain. If there are no significant changes today, he may be able to escape danger. According to the condition report released by Fumin Hospital yesterday, at 2 AM yesterday morning, the temperature was 38 degrees, the pulse was 96, and the respiration was 20. At 5 AM, it was 38.5 degrees, the pulse was 100, and the respiration was 28. At 8 AM, it was 38.6 degrees, the pulse was 96, and the respiration was 26. At 11 AM, it was 38.4 degrees, the pulse was 94, and the respiration was 22. At 2 PM, it was 38.9 degrees, the pulse was 96, and the respiration was 24. At 9 PM, the temperature was 39 degrees. As for Consul General Murai, since yesterday morning, his temperature has decreased to 37.4 degrees, and he is expected to gradually recover.

The End Is Near for the Traitors of Zhabei

The Zhabei traitors Hu Lifu, Wang Du, etc., seeing that the ceasefire agreement has been signed and established, and that all areas of Zhabei will soon be taken over by the municipal government and police authority will be restored, are extremely panicked. Thus, the traitors who relied on the power of the Japanese military have now fallen into a dead end. Letters from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Municipal Federation of Trade Unions, etc., Regarding the Preparation of National Crisis Savings Funds

Because Long-Term Savings Funds Are Different from Temporary Fundraising

Increasing Members' Burdens Requires Submission to the General Assembly According to Law

The National Crisis Savings Fund initiated by the Citizens' Joint Association and other organizations, after sending personnel to contact various circles, has seen a continuous stream of enthusiastic responses. Although the time has not been long, the results have already been quite impressive. The association had previously sent representatives to request the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to send personnel to participate in the preparations. Yesterday, the Chamber of Commerce replied to the association, stating, "In reply, we have received your letter requesting approval of the preparation committee for the National Crisis Savings Fund, etc. This case was first brought up for discussion at the 91st regular meeting of our Chamber on the 2nd of this month. It was unanimously agreed that saving funds to save the country is a preparation for long-term resistance against Japan, and in principle, it is absolutely agreed. Furthermore, our Chamber has previously had resolutions regarding the preparation fund for the war against Japan and the contribution of various industries. However, long-term savings funds are different from temporary fundraising in terms of approach. According to the Commercial Association Law and the Trade Association Law, increasing members' burdens must be approved by the members' general meeting, and the undertaking must concentrate the power of various industries in order to achieve satisfactory and grand results. It is proposed that the executive committee submit this case to the members' general meeting for discussion, etc." After deliberation, it was submitted to the 24th meeting of the executive committee of our Chamber on May 6, and with the endorsement of Executive Committee Member Wu Zhihao, it was passed in accordance with the opinion of the standing committee. We are now replying to your letter, please take note accordingly.

The 19th Route Army Will Hold a Memorial Service for Fallen Soldiers on a Regular Basis

Location: Suzhou

Date: May 20th

Since the night of January 28th, when the brutal Japanese began their invasion and started the war in Zhabei, Shanghai, the 19th Route Army, fulfilling its duty as soldiers to defend the country and its territory, bravely resisted, maneuvering with the enemy, charging and fighting hand-to-hand, venturing in and out of a hail of bullets. It has now been more than three months. There have undoubtedly been many loyal and brave soldiers who have died under the artillery fire of the brutal Japanese. The 19th Route Army Organizes an Air Force

With Zhang Huichang as Air Force Commander, and Ding Jixu as Deputy

Divided into Five Squadrons: Reconnaissance, Bombing, Pursuit, Combat, and Cover

Since the outbreak of the Shanghai Incident, and the 19th Route Army's active resistance against Japan, Commander-in-Chief Jiang Guangnai and Army Commander Cai Tingkai have sent telegrams to overseas Chinese around the world, soliciting donations of airplanes to facilitate the resistance against Japan. Aviation Commander Zhang Huichang of Guangdong has also sent personnel to various places to personally solicit donations, with excellent results. A total of more than 120 aircraft have been raised and are being shipped back to the country in batches. However, the overseas Chinese have repeatedly and solemnly declared that these aircraft should be used exclusively for foreign defense or bandit suppression and should not participate in domestic operations. According to reliable information from the Shanghai office of the 19th Route Army, Commander-in-Chief Jiang Guangnai and Army Commander Cai Tingkai believe that in this battle against Japan, the 19th Route Army suffered heavy losses due to the lack of an air force. It has now been decided to establish an air squadron of the 19th Route Army with the aircraft donated by overseas Chinese, with Zhang Huichang as the air force commander and Ding Jixu as the deputy commander. The organizational structure is divided into five squadrons: reconnaissance, bombing, pursuit, combat, and cover, with a number of aircraft in each squadron, evenly distributed among the more than 120 aircraft. If overseas Chinese continue to donate in the future, they will all be added to the combat and bombing squadrons to strengthen their strength. This time, when Zhang Huichang came to Shanghai from Guangdong, Jiang and Cai entrusted Zhang to handle this plan with full authority. Once approved by the central government, organization can begin. According to personnel from the Shanghai office of the 19th Route Army, after the air squadron is approved and successfully organized by the central government, it will not participate in any internal warfare other than resisting foreign aggression and suppressing bandits, in order to live up to the expectations of the overseas Chinese.

The Food Commission Held a Regular Meeting Yesterday

The Municipal Food Commission held its 33rd regular meeting at 2 PM on May 7 at the Bureau of Social Affairs. Twelve people attended, including Zhang Binghui, Sun Yongyi, Zhu Zixiang, Yu Zixiang, and Yan Xiaoquan. Zhang Binghui chaired the meeting, and Zhou Minggang recorded the minutes. First, the chairman reported: (1) Due to the situation, the meeting was suspended twice, and thereafter, the regular meeting will still be held once a month as usual. (2) Recently, there have been too many rice and grain exports. For the sake of prudent food supply, and in accordance with the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office's request for joint restrictions, the rice and grain export registration method has been revised. If rice merchants come to Shanghai to handle rice, and the local governments do not directly send official documents to the Bureau of Social Affairs, they must provide proof from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce or the Rice and Grain Trade Association or a certified public accountant. (3) Recently, the rice and grain trade association, which sells rice and grain, has requested the issuance of passports for rice and grain purchased from the interior. However, the Bureau of Social Affairs believes that the municipal government also issues rice transportation passports, which is unavoidable. The bureau is currently requesting instructions for a unified method and will reply after receiving instructions. (4) The transportation expenses for expert committee members were temporarily suspended due to the city treasury's shortfall. Now that the situation has recovered, it is planned to submit a request to the municipal government to approve the continuation of the previous allocation. As for the discussion items, it was resolved: (1) The survey and statistics of rice and grain in this city will continue to be carried out. In addition to requesting the Bureau of Social Affairs to send personnel to investigate, the Rice Industry Association will be asked to assist in reporting. (2) Rice ships transporting rice to Shanghai from the interior are often detained by the military, which greatly affects the food supply. It was decided to submit a request to the municipal government to forward it to the Ministry of Military Affairs and the Military Commission to instruct all armies in the front to release all ships holding the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs' rice transportation flag. (3) Regarding the export of rice and grain, in addition to proof from the local government and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce or the rice industry group and certified public accountants, the Bureau of Social Affairs is requested to formulate a certificate format for distribution to various rice industry groups. After the rice industry groups are responsible for verification, it can be released.

According to reports, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a request to the Bureau of Social Affairs to change the rice and grain export registration method. Yesterday, the person in charge of the bureau stated, "Regarding the export of rice and grain in this city, rice merchants have always held rice transportation passports from local governments, which are stamped by the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office, and then apply for registration with the bureau. The bureau previously received a letter from the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office stating that since the Japanese army forcibly occupied Zhabei, Liuhe, and other places, rice and grain exports from this city have suddenly increased. In one month, the rice and grain transported to Tong, Chong, and Hai have totaled more than 10,000 dan. In order to prevent aiding the enemy and exporting it to other places, it is proposed to jointly restrict it. The bureau checked the registered quantity of rice and grain exports, and the quantity of rice and grain exports in March and April was double the export quantity of the previous year. In order to prevent abuses, the registration method was changed. That is, for all rice and grain exports, in addition to having passports from various governments, there must also be a direct telegram from the government to this bureau for verification. If this procedure is not available, there must be a certificate issued by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce or the Rice and Grain Trade Association or a certified public accountant in Shanghai to prove it. This regulation is designed to be prudent about the food supply, so the inclusion of the certified public accountant item was originally intended to facilitate rice merchants to obtain proof from more places. Certified public accountants can handle or certify all documents or events in commercial affairs, and it is not inappropriate in principle. If it is said that certified public accountants charge public fees, this is a matter of personal business and is not this bureau opening up a way for certified public accountants to make a fortune. This bureau has not stipulated that all certificates must be issued by certified public accountants and that fees must be paid. If rice merchants want to be free, they can ask the Municipal Chamber of Commerce or the Rice and Grain Trade Association for certification. This bureau has never delayed registration. For example, the North City Office of the Bean and Rice Industry Association and Mr. Gu Xinyi, a member of the standing committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, submitted certificates to the bureau, which were stamped immediately. As for the so-called different proofs and different treatments in the news, it is not known what it is based on. The registration method of this bureau is entirely based on principles and is not inconvenient for merchants and people. For the sake of prudent food supply, it should be handled in accordance with the newly revised method and never be easily changed."

The Anti-Opium Association Again Cables Zhang Xueliang

Public Sales in North China Provinces Have Become Concrete Realities

Questions Whether Telegram to Tianjin Association Is Based on Denial

The Chinese National Anti-Opium Association reported yesterday that Hebei Pacification Director Zhang Xueliang had cabled to deny the implementation of public opium sales in the four provinces of North China. The Anti-Opium Association believes that it is necessary to thoroughly understand the truth in this matter and has again cabled Zhang Xueliang to inquire about the beginning and end of the matter. The original text is recorded as follows: "Urgent delivery to Mr. Zhang Hanqing, Hebei Pacification Director. The previous telegram should have arrived and been noted. Now, according to the report from the Hebei Anti-Opium Association, regarding the implementation of public opium sales in the four provinces of North China, you telegraphed the association, strongly denying it. The association was first happy to hear this, but then became confused. We were happy because you advocated opium prohibition and have not changed your original intention. We were confused because the obvious facts are like this and seem difficult to erase. According to recent newspaper reports, public opium sales have indeed been implemented in the four provinces under your jurisdiction. The opium delivered to Tianjin has reached more than 3,000 tons, and the rest is still being transported. The official opium sales agency in Hebei Province is the Northern Company, a powerful organization initially established in the Third Special District. Later, because the transportation of opium passed through the Italian Concession and 60,000 taels were seized, it was moved to the Second Special District. When opium arrives in Tianjin, it is unloaded at the new station, and destruction certificates are issued. People who sell and transport opium purchase certificates and can pass without hindrance. Police and soldiers must protect them. Each destruction certificate costs two yuan, and one certificate is affixed to each package of opium weighing twenty taels, which can be used in this area. If it is transported from this area to another area, the fee is doubled. If the police and soldiers inspect the destruction certificate in transit and the amount affixed is insufficient, a double penalty will be imposed. Thus, Sui opium is sold smoothly in the Pingjin area. The fundraising committee, in order to plan for the long term, is afraid that after official sales, the number of addicts will increase and the source will be limited. For a long time, the supply will not meet the demand. Therefore, it is proposed to order the county magistrates to persuade farmers to plant opium, which will not only avoid a lack of supply but also allow the collection of opium taxes. All of the above measures are symbols of public sales. Openly collecting taxes, persuading farmers to plant opium, issuing destruction certificates with the nature of stamps, eating, selling, transporting, and planting are all free from the law. Police and soldiers also have the obligation to protect them. The concrete state of public opium sales has already adopted everything, without exception. What has not been used is only to avoid the name of public sales. It is completely contrary to your telegram, which is very confusing. In the past, the area where opium prohibition was best handled in our country, the Northeast, achieved the most prominent results. This association was proud of it, believing that meat eaters are not necessarily all incapable of planning. Unexpectedly, the Mukden Incident occurred, and you retreated to Pingjin. The blows you suffered were too deep, and your views also wavered as a result, reversing your previous determination to implement opium prohibition and coveting the evil system of public opium sales. This cannot but make those who love you heartbroken and those who hate you more critical. I hope that you will act decisively, exert your wisdom, and immediately withdraw your order, abolish the public sales system, and severely punish those who advocate traitors to prevent disaster and protect your reputation. Your sincere heart hopes for your understanding. Respectfully, the Chinese National Anti-Opium Association, Yang."

Declaration of the Shanghai Bar Association

Correcting Macnaghten's Speech

On April 13 of this year, the Western taxpayers of the Shanghai Public Concession held an annual meeting. Macnaghten, the chairman of the Municipal Council, vigorously attacked the First Special District Court when reporting on the administrative situation of the concession in the past year. The points of his attack can be roughly divided into two points. First, after September 18, the court turned a blind eye to the boycott of Japanese goods, which led to the Sino-Japanese Zhabei War. Therefore, the court was deemed to have failed in its duty. Second, foreign merchants were very dissatisfied with the court's civil cases, and the annual speech of the chairman of the Harmony Merchants' Association was used as proof. It was also hoped that after the current agreement expires, an international court could be organized to replace the existing court, and that uniform civil and criminal laws could be implemented for residents within the concession, regardless of nationality. Macnaghten's report on the situation of the court that day was roughly like this. This association feels that it is necessary to correct such fallacies that are not legal or factual and specially refutes them as follows. According to this, Japan used its naval, land, and air forces to invade Shanghai, which was a step planned for its entire policy of aggression against China. Anyone who is familiar with the situation in the Far East can see this. Therefore, it is not true that the Chinese boycott of Japanese goods was the fuse for the Japanese aggression. Otherwise, Mayor Wu would have unconditionally succumbed to the beautiful note of his naval commander on January 28, and one of the conditions of surrender was to disband the anti-Japanese national salvation association. If the Japanese regarded the anti-Japanese movement as the reason for their use of force, they would have been complacent and silently rested. However, the blood was not yet dry, and the smoke of war suddenly rose. A good market was turned into ashes. What was the intention? There is no need for our people to investigate. However, Macnaghten actually placed the responsibility for this war on the First Special District Court, not only ignoring the general trend in the Far East but also obliterating the local situation. Furthermore, according to our country's laws, the court does not hear criminal cases unless they are reported, and the Special District Court is restricted by the agreement, that is, the prosecutor's right to sue is almost completely deprived. The person who holds the criminal prosecution power in the Public Concession is the Municipal Council Police Department. According to the court's statement the day before yesterday, the Municipal Council only prosecuted three cases related to the anti-Japanese movement, and all of them were legally judged by the court. Some were acquitted due to insufficient evidence, and some were fined due to minor circumstances. Benevolence and knowledge are seen, and the judges have the power to make their own judgments. How can they be judged to have failed in their duty because the legal judgment failed to meet the hopes of a small number of citizens in the area? This kind of argument can be tolerated if it comes from the mouth of an ignorant person. But now it is seen in the speech of the person sitting in the position of the chairman of the Municipal Council at the annual meeting of Western taxpayers, talking eloquently and making wild remarks. This is something that members of this association cannot but regret. It is heard that one of the cases is in the process of appeal, and the police department is still in the position of the plaintiff. However, the responsible person of the police department's superior agency publicly criticized how unfair the judgment was and how partial the judge was. It is obvious that they are trying to use political power to suppress the judiciary. It is impossible not to be surprised and disappointed. Furthermore, in Macnaghten's speech, he spared no effort to attack how the Anti-Japanese Association was engaged in private gain and corruption. The organization of the Anti-Japanese Association is a patriotic movement of the people. Whether it should exist or not does not involve the scope of the law and does not need to be elaborated. If its behavior is truly out of line, it should also be reported by the police department in accordance with the law, and then the court can hear and judge it. Now, only two cases have been reported by the police department, and neither of them involves the Anti-Japanese Association itself. Now, why is the court blamed for not enforcing the law to rope it in? Why is it strict in blaming others and lenient in blaming oneself? Therefore, based on the above, it is more appropriate to say that the police department failed in its duty than to say that the court failed in its duty. As for foreign merchants' dissatisfaction with civil cases, the points of dissatisfaction are not stated. Aimless, there is no value in answering. Looking closely at Macnaghten's speech, the most important focus is to establish an international court in the Public Concession. This is his attack on the Special District Court and his criticism of China's judiciary. He uses the theory of innocence as a step to support his own arguments. If this is the case, then why not say it directly? Why go around in circles and use our country's dignified legal system as a sacrifice for his speech? This is not what the people of a country ruled by law should do. In short, what our colleagues cannot say to Macnaghten and all the Western directors and citizens of the Municipal Council is that if you want the safety and prosperity of the Shanghai Public Concession, the rule of law is the first priority. If you want to promote the rule of law, then eliminating power is the first priority. This responsibility should be borne entirely by the Municipal Council. But in this incident, the Japanese navy, army, and air force used the concession as a base for operations, which already violated the treaty, and the ronin and hooligans acted as accomplices, committing all kinds of evil. It is not known how many Chinese people were slaughtered, raped, and killed, and it is not known how many people were kidnapped and disappeared. The property of Chinese and foreigners suffered losses due to this Japanese invasion, and the value is more than tens of millions of yuan. The law is equal to invalidity, and the treaties have all become waste paper. It has not been heard that the Municipal Council has protested in one incident or prosecuted in one case. The rule of law that Chinese and foreigners have longed for has fallen to an all-time low and entered a point of no return. Our colleagues are deeply saddened by this. Why did Macnaghten and the Western directors not mention a word about it at the current annual meeting of Western taxpayers? This is truly what is called seeing the small and abandoning the big, knowing the near and forgetting the far. If this kind of erroneous view is not changed one day, then the future of the concession's security will be worrying one day, and the goal of the rule of law will not be achieved one day. Macnaghten has gone, and may the Western directors of the current session encourage themselves well.

Workers at the Qiuxin Shipyard, dissatisfied with the management's violation of labor-management agreements and various forms of oppression, have launched a strike. Detective Killed While Arresting Thieves, Eight Notorious Robbers Captured

Detective Jin's Funeral Set for Tomorrow

Police Station Will Provide Compensation to the Bereaved Family

Qian Achun Dies from Severe Injuries

Trial of Eight Robbers Postponed

Jin Baoyi, a probationary detective from Siyang who had recently been promoted to Detective Number 61 at the French Concession Police, was patrolling with fellow officers at 8:20 PM when they encountered three suspected criminals at the intersection of Avenue de la Victoire and Rue de Bayle. The suspects opened fire, injuring Jin in the head, killing him instantly, and wounding passersby with stray bullets. Fellow officers and patrolmen pursued and captured one of the suspects, seizing a Mauser pistol with nineteen rounds of ammunition. The suspect was taken to the police station, and Jin's body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Parlor for an autopsy. The injured passersby were sent to the hospital for treatment. Details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that the captured suspect identified himself as Wang Ziqing, age 28, from Anhui Province. He also revealed the hiding places of his accomplices. Special agents, including Detective Inspector Jin Jiulin, Chief Detective Li Yaolong, Mao Jingen, Deputy Detective Zhang Ziying, and Qian Yumin, led a full complement of armed officers, along with detectives from the Second Branch of the Second District of the Chinese Public Safety Bureau, to No. 2 Lanfang Lane, Zhaojiabang Road at midnight. There, they arrested Liu Biao, Wang Shoujing, and Zheng Chang, all from Hunan Province. Waiting until 2:00 AM, they apprehended Fu Shunqing and Fu Panmin, both from Shandong Province, who arrived at the location. They were all taken to the police station. Later, in collaboration with Chinese and Western detectives from the Public Concession Police, they proceeded to Room 38 of the Lin'an Hotel at No. 257 Jiu'an Lane, Guangdong Road, and captured Wang Yousheng and Yu Juxing, both from Zhejiang Province. A handgun and seven rounds of ammunition were found on the roof of the hotel and confiscated. The suspects were taken to the police station for investigation. Yesterday morning, Wu Xiaoke, the prosecutor from the Second Special District Court, accompanied by forensic doctor Jiang Xuan and clerk Zhao Yifen, arrived at the police station after being informed by the Criminal Division of the General Police Station. They examined the body and convened a formal hearing. Detective Bao presented the details of the case. Jin Wangshi, the deceased detective's wife, filed a request for redress. The defendants were escorted to the case by police detectives. After questioning by the prosecutor, it was determined that Jin Douyi (Jin Baoyi) had indeed died from gunshot wounds sustained before his death. The body was released to his wife, Jin Wangshi, for funeral arrangements. The defendants were handed over to the police for further investigation. After the autopsy, at 11:00 AM, the police escorted the eight defendants to the Second Special District Court. Judge Li Changnian, accompanied by clerk Wu Shan, presided over the hearing in the First Criminal Court. First, the police lawyer Gu Shouxi presented the case, stating that at approximately 8:00 PM the previous night, detectives from

Page 10

the Police Station were inspecting pedestrians for criminals on Avenue de la Victoire when they were fired upon by the defendants, resulting in the death of Detective Jin Baoyi from a headshot and injuries to bystanders from stray bullets. Only one defendant and seven of his accomplices were apprehended. The police are charging them with obstructing official duties, murder, and robbery under Articles 142(3), 282, and 348 of the Criminal Code. The police still need to thoroughly investigate whether the defendants have committed other crimes. Due to time constraints, the police requested a postponement of the trial for two weeks. The seized Mauser pistol and ammunition were presented as evidence. Judge Li briefly questioned the defendants and announced that the trial would be postponed to May 21st. The defendants were temporarily detained at the police station. Qian Achun, also known as A Lin, the bystander who was injured by a stray bullet, age 35, from Changzhou, and working as a dockworker, was sent to Guangci Hospital. Due to severe abdominal injuries, treatment was ineffective, and he died at 10:00 AM yesterday. The hospital notified the police, who took the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Parlor for an autopsy. As his address was unknown, his family could not be located. The court will be notified tomorrow to conduct an inspection. Wu Yuexiang, a tailor, age 33, from Taicang, sustained minor injuries and is being treated at Renji Hospital. He is expected to recover soon. The detective's body will be placed in a coffin today and the funeral will be held tomorrow. At 1:00 PM, the procession will depart from the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Parlor, proceed west on Xixinqiao Street, north on Avenue Edward VII, west on Avenue Petain, turn onto Avenue de la Victoire, and south on Rue de Bayle, directly to the Yiji Shanhui in the Chinese area for temporary storage. A date will be chosen later to transport the remains back to his hometown for burial. His colleagues and police staff commend Jin's bravery and dedication to public service and will raise funds to support his family. All will attend the funeral.

Sister Sues Brother with Tears, Brother Remains Unmoved

Father Left an Estate of Nearly a Million

Court Awards Five Thousand Yuan, Brother Refuses to Pay

Siblings Continue to Litigate

Judge Urges Reconciliation

Hu Disheng, manager of the Xinyun Money Exchange, and his brother, Hu Runsheng, both shareholders of the Yida Money Exchange and both from Yuyao, were sued last year by their sister, Hu Shanshan, for neglect of support. According to the complaint, Shanshan was only seven months old when her father, Youxiang, passed away, leaving an estate of nearly a million. The estate was managed by her eldest brother, Disheng, and second brother, Lansheng. Disheng was born to the first wife, Zhou, while Lansheng and Shanshan were born to Cheng. The plaintiff claimed that she had a hard life and is now over thirty years old. After her two elder brothers divided the property and lived separately, she lived with her biological mother at Lansheng's residence. However, the plaintiff has vowed to remain single and works at the Nanyang Women's Middle School to support herself. Now, more than thirty years after her father's death, she does not have the right to demand a share of the estate. However, since the plaintiff is determined not to marry and has no ability to support herself, based on the precedents of the Supreme Court cases 5Shang318, 3Shang669, and 7Shang761, she is entitled to request that the defendants assume the obligation of support or provide a living allowance. Therefore, she requested a judgment ordering the two defendants to pay 100,000 yuan in alimony. After investigation by the First Special District Court, the court concluded that the amount requested by the plaintiff was excessive. After considering the defendants' ability, the court ordered them to pay the plaintiff 5,000 yuan in cash. Hu Lansheng expressed his satisfaction with this judgment. However, Hu Disheng refused to pay even a single cent. He hired a lawyer to file an appeal with the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, claiming that Shanshan had no right to claim support and that she lived with her mother, whose food and clothing were provided by Lansheng, which means she was already being supported. He further argued that the appellant had no ability to pay and requested that the original judgment be dismissed. Hu Shanshan, because her elder brother did not accept the original judgment and filed an appeal, also hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to defend her case and filed a cross-appeal, insisting that the court order the defendants to comply with the original judgment and pay her 50,000 yuan in cash. Her reasons were as follows: Shanshan is alone and has not received adequate education and lacks specialized skills. She is only thirty years old and has a long life ahead of her. Her mother will eventually pass away, and she has no reliable relatives. If she does not seek support, how will she maintain her livelihood? Lansheng's economic status is far less than that of Disheng. He is also kind enough to accept the judgment out of brotherly love. Only Disheng is cruel and has control of the vast estate of their ancestors but has not provided support or education to his biological mother and sister, leaving Shanshan without skills and alone. He is now unwilling to pay the small amount ordered by the court and has filed an appeal, further demonstrating his unreasonableness. Furthermore, according to Disheng, their deceased father's will was forged by Lansheng. Regarding this point, she is currently collecting evidence and preparing to file a criminal lawsuit. She requested that the appeal be rejected and the original verdict be changed, ordering Disheng to pay 50,000 yuan in cash. Yesterday, Presiding Judge Hu Min of the Second Branch of the High Court, along with judges Han and Ye, held a hearing. They first questioned Hu Disheng about the reasons for his appeal. Hu claimed that he had no ability to pay and requested that the original judgment be dismissed. He further stated that his deceased father's estate was only over 30,000 yuan, and after deducting the expenses for his father's death and funeral, only 28,900 taels remained. Judge Hu then asked Disheng, "If you have no ability to pay now, will you fulfill the original judgment when you have the ability in the future?" Disheng hesitated and said, "This will have to be determined in the future." Judge Hu then advised him, "Siblings litigating against each other is not only frowned upon by traditional morality, but also detrimental to good customs in this modern era. Why do you value money more than your siblings?" He then urged them to seek reconciliation to end the dispute. However, Disheng did not make any concrete expression. The court then questioned Hu Shanshan, who tearfully stated that her elder brother definitely had assets and had deposits in banks such as the Bank of China and the Continental Bank, but it was not easy to investigate. She wept, her appearance likened to a pear blossom in the rain. After the lawyers for both parties had finished their arguments, the court announced that the verdict would be announced at a later date. The judge again earnestly advised both parties and their lawyers to reconcile outside the court. If a peaceful resolution can be reached before the date of the verdict, it can be avoided by legal judgment. The Hu siblings then withdrew with their lawyers.

Recent Updates on the Riyie Bank Case Handled by City Government Volunteer Lawyers

Creditors Should Pay Litigation Fees Quickly

The case of creditors suing to recover deposits from Shanghai Riyie Bank and Dashijie Amusement Savings Department has been legally pursued by volunteer lawyers Jiang Yiping, Chen Tingrui, Qin Liankui, and Wu Jingxiong, appointed by the city government. Creditors have already received two installments of the distributed payments. However, in the part of the case filed in the former French Court, the court ruled that Ye Shantao and others were exempt from shareholder and director liability, which is inconsistent with the facts. After the appeal was filed to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, it was ruled that the litigation fees of more than 7,000 yuan were required to be paid. Because the creditors had financial difficulties and no money to advance, they had to explain the situation and request permission to use legal aid. The court refused to grant the request, and the petition was dismissed. An appeal was filed to the Supreme Court, but it was also rejected. After that, a ruling was received from the High Court urging the payment of the litigation fees. At that time, the Japanese army invaded and the war was raging. Two requests were made to the court for an extension, and the four lawyers published notices in various newspapers, urging creditors to pay the litigation fees within ten days, calculated at one percent of the original amount of the claim, so that they could be collected and submitted to the court to avoid unfavorable judgments due to incomplete appeal procedures. After seeing the notice in the newspapers, creditors actively went to the four lawyers' offices to pay the litigation fees. Every day, a significant amount of litigation fees was remitted from other locations. In addition, many letters were received requesting an extension or a postponement. In order to protect the interests of the creditors, the four lawyers requested the court for one last extension. A ruling has now been received extending the deadline to the 20th of this month. Before the 20th, if there are any creditors of Shanghai Riyie Bank and Dashijie Amusement Savings Department "who have registered at the lawyers' office designated by the city government" or "who have registered at the creditors' group on Lloyd Road," and who have not yet paid the litigation fees, they can bring their deposit slips to the four lawyers' offices and continue to pay the litigation fees at one percent of the total amount of the claim. Those who have already registered in other locations can also clearly state the type, number, date, and amount of the claim and remit the litigation fees to the four lawyers' offices so that they can be collected and submitted to the court to obtain legal remedies.

Extension of Public Bus Route No. 2

The public bus company, in view of the fact that many residents in the northern district have now moved to the south of Avenue Foch and Avenue Edward VII, and there is no direct bus route from that area to the northern district, is planning to extend the existing public bus route No. 2 from Hongkou Park to Two-Mile Creek Bridge on Avenue Edward VII westward, via Avenue Edward VII, Avenue Foch, and Avenue Haig, to the vicinity of the Georg Hotel. New Police Station in the Eastern District

The eastern district of the Public Concession, east of Huishan Road, has been developing rapidly in recent years. However, there is only one police station in that area, the Yangshupu Police Station at the corner of Yangshupu Road and Lan Road. Its jurisdiction is very large, and the police station is one and a half miles away from the eastern boundary. In view of this, the Public Works Department has built a new police station at the corner of Yulin Road and Weituoma Road, and another new police station at the corner of Gelan Road and Pingliang Road. The police station on Yulin Road has been completed and will begin operations on May 15th. The jurisdiction of the new police station extends to the Yangshupu River. The area east of the river will still be managed by the Yangshupu Police Station. The new police stations are built with steel and reinforced concrete, with four floors in one part and five floors in another. They are equipped with steam pipes and sanitary facilities. The lower floor has offices, storage rooms, detention centers, workshops, garages, etc. The upper floors have dormitories for police officers, including three units with four rooms and four units with three rooms for Western officers. There are also 16 single rooms, a dining room, and a recreation room. For Japanese officers, there are 16 units with three rooms and three single rooms. For Indian and Chinese officers, there is accommodation for 28 Indian officers and 78 Chinese officers. In addition, there are dining rooms and accommodations for 36 servants. The garage can accommodate five cars. The construction of the new police station on Gelan Road started later and is expected to be completed by the end of this year. Once it is opened, the current Yangshupu Police Station will be closed. The Yangshupu Police Station was established in 1891. It has two floors. Forty years ago, when the population was small, it was sufficient.
